  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_1db7a0db-2bb9-4180-849c-433f0f18ad43'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText5128887545455102822" style="display:none">The twisty, gripping number one bestseller from Richard and Judy Book Club winner Clare Mackintosh, author of I Let You Go.<br /><br /><b>Winner of the Richard and Judy Summer Book Club 2017</b><br /><br />When Zoe Walker sees her photo in the classifieds section of a London newspaper, she is determined to find out why it's there. There's no explanation: just a grainy image, a website address and a phone number. She takes it home to her family, who are convinced it's just someone who looks like Zoe. But the next day the advert shows a photo of a different woman, and another the day after that.<br /><br />Is it a mistake? A coincidence? Or is someone keeping track of every move they make...<br /><br />If you like Shari Lapena, Paula Hawkins, Rachel Abbott, B A Paris, Fiona Barton, Ruth Ware and CL Taylor, you'll love this gripping psychological thriller.</span>

<div class='communityQuestionSubTitle'>
Popular Answered Questions

<div id='communityQuestionsWithAnswers'>
<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/836940-i-ve-just-started-listening-to-the-book">I&#39;ve just started listening to the book and it is just about driving me up the wall that three of the characters are named; Kathy, Kelly and Katie. 
Why is it nessecary to pick so simelar names, when there are so many to choose between???</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_836940'><a id="like_count_community_question_836940" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/836940?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">64 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F26233572-i-see-you">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/836940-i-ve-just-started-listening-to-the-book">4 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/836940-i-ve-just-started-listening-to-the-book">See all 9 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/37914925-kira"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1419399562i/37914925._UY100_CR3,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/37914925-kira">Kira</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It is an author's responsibility to choose names that are easily distinguishable from one another, and an editor's job to make sure the author has don<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It is an author's responsibility to choose names that are easily distinguishable from one another, and an editor's job to make sure the author has done his/her job. This situation should never have gotten all the way to the publication stage without being corrected. Unfortunately editing seems to be a lost skill these days. In addition to problems like this, I have read many, many books that are anywhere from 50 to 100 pages too long. If you're writing a memoir, take your time and describe the scenery if you want. If you're writing a mystery or thriller, evaluate each word, each sentence, each paragraph, and determine whether it moves the story forward or slows it down. If it slows it down, take it out!<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=suspense-mystery-thriller">suspense-mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=not-for-me">not-for-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=too-much-hype">too-much-hype</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1523362172" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16653484609209650047">Turns out, it might be harder to write a second novel than a debut. I’ve actually heard, quite a few times now, that second books can be a beast. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8509533.Clare_Mackintosh' title='Clare Mackintosh' rel='nofollow noopener'>Clare Mackintosh</a> even takes the time to mention that in the acknowledgements of this book. I imagine it's even more so coming off of a debut as heart-pounding and impressive as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23125266.I_Let_You_Go' title='I Let You Go by Clare Mackintosh' rel='nofollow noopener'>I Let You Go</a>. Naturally, that’s where my thoughts went—would Ms. Mackintosh be able to emulate the shock value and sheer brilliance of that masterpiece?<br/><br/>For me, I LET YOU GO was </span>
  <span id="freeText16653484609209650047" style="display:none">Turns out, it might be harder to write a second novel than a debut. I’ve actually heard, quite a few times now, that second books can be a beast. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8509533.Clare_Mackintosh" title="Clare Mackintosh" rel="nofollow noopener">Clare Mackintosh</a> even takes the time to mention that in the acknowledgements of this book. I imagine it's even more so coming off of a debut as heart-pounding and impressive as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23125266.I_Let_You_Go" title="I Let You Go by Clare Mackintosh" rel="nofollow noopener">I Let You Go</a>. Naturally, that’s where my thoughts went—would Ms. Mackintosh be able to emulate the shock value and sheer brilliance of that masterpiece?<br /><br />For me, I LET YOU GO was a stunner. The unforeseen twist in that story knocked me on my ass. It’s still a standout in my mind, over a year and hundreds of books later, and one that I’ve measured other psychological thrillers against, time and time again. Including this one. Just in case you don’t fully grasp how spectacular I found that book to be, a pristine signed copy has garnered a coveted spot on my bookshelf among the few others I’ve considered worthy over the years.<br /><br />This one on the other hand, not so much. <b>The most exciting part of this entire book was the epilogue.</b> Hands down. Had it not been for that last ditch effort to shock her readers with a much needed twist, my rating would have been a little different.<br /><br />Sure, the thought of being watched and followed was anxiety inducing—in the beginning. The author relies too heavily on that fear to carry this story and without much action, the payoff doesn’t feel big enough. At least not for this suspense junkie. I’m sorry to say, but I found the majority of Zoe and Kelly’s story to be <b>incredibly slow, rife with convenience, clunky with awkward revelations and just not all that exciting.</b> Besides Kelly, there wasn’t a whole lot of depth to any of these characters.<br /><br />What happened? I had to sit back and consider, was it that my hopes for this one were too high? Was I just another passenger on the expectation train unfairly demanding the same experience her first novel delivered? Maybe, but I’m not sure it mattered. I think regardless of who wrote this book, my feelings would have been the same. There wasn’t anything about these characters or the plot that I found compelling, noteworthy or even believable.<br /><br /><b>Was it just me or did the entire plot hinge on an idea that seemed pretty unlikely?</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I struggled with the whole—find the one dot com—scenario. If you’re a crazed stalker that’s looking for a victim to watch, assault or murder, would you really turn to a website to provide the details of a woman’s daily commute on a train? Granted, I’m no expert on the subject, but in my mind, I imagine any psycho with those inclinations would handpick their victim, probably after a chance meeting, and subsequently do the legwork themselves. Haven’t we learned from all the movies, true crime shows and books out there that selecting victims and learning their routine is all part of the ritual? So would a man with that disposition just skip the foreplay and go straight for the kill by using some website disguised as a dating site instead? I don’t think so. It didn’t seem plausible to me that anyone would use this “service”, let alone pay for it or even take the time to try and crack the coded password.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> The author provided an explanation within the story, but unfortunately it wasn’t enough to get this reader on board. <br /><br /><i>*THANK YOU to Berkley and NetGalley for an ARC in exchange for an honest review.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="16653484609209650047" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1803808870" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1803808870" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1803808870?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781101988299" href="/book/show/31160324-i-see-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=from-publisher-or-author">from-publisher-or-author</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1803808870" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6880700971717625141">this is a fun thriller, but it requires the reader to accept its premise without questioning its logic, and to suspend disbelief like a mofo. if you can do that, you'll have a good time. if you cannot, this is not the book for you. <br/><br/>i can medium do it, so while i enjoyed reading this for the rush and the whodunnit of it all, there were just certain things i could not look past as a reader. it's one of those page-turnery books i loved at the time of reading, but it's forgettable and a little silly</span>
  <span id="freeText6880700971717625141" style="display:none">this is a fun thriller, but it requires the reader to accept its premise without questioning its logic, and to suspend disbelief like a mofo. if you can do that, you'll have a good time. if you cannot, this is not the book for you. <br><br>i can medium do it, so while i enjoyed reading this for the rush and the whodunnit of it all, there were just certain things i could not look past as a reader. it's one of those page-turnery books i loved at the time of reading, but it's forgettable and a little silly after it's all over. <br><br>it's a psychological suspense novel and it's one whose goal is to take the quotidian and creepify it, so the reader is left unsettled and uneasy in a familiar, taken-for-granted part of their daily life. this one focuses on the already-harrowing experience of public transportation, casting a sinister light on the straphanging lifestyle. which, yes, is what <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22557272.The_Girl_on_the_Train" title="The Girl on the Train by Paula Hawkins" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl on the Train</a> did, but this is completely its own thing, although paula hawkins does blurb it, because british transportation-based thriller writing women gotta stick together.<br><br>zoe walker is stuck on a stalled train during her commute home one night, forced to read the parts of the paper she wouldn't ordinarily in her desperation for diversion, when she notices a photo of herself in a classified ad with no information other than a phone number and a web address: findtheone.com. naturally confused and concerned, once she gets home she tries to get to the bottom of it, but the number is a dead end, and the site requires a password. her grown children and live-in boyfriend don't share her alarm - assuring her that the small picture might be of someone else entirely, and zoe reluctantly concedes, although she is still a bit apprehensive. when she discovers that a woman whose picture ran in the same ad space was later murdered, her dread grows and she contacts the police, who do not take her concerns seriously until the pattern continues and zoe finds herself in real danger. <br><br>the story is split narratively between zoe and kelly swift, a detective demoted to smalltime police work after assaulting a rape suspect, who has been trying to claw her way back to the big leagues ever since. she sees connections between zoe's story and a pickpocketing crime she's been assigned, and she insinuates herself into the case, thrilled to be investigating real crimes once more, eager to impress the other detectives and shed her tarnished reputation. which does not mean that she's going to play it cool and careful - for all the strong contributions she makes to the investigation, she also behaves unprofessionally a number of times, compromising the case and making more enemies.<br><br>in the tradition of psychological suspense, paranoia grows throughout the novel, and suspicion is cast on many people close to zoe, increasing her anxiety and leaving her with no one to trust. many red herrings, many tense situations, much atmospheric dread. <br><br>and also a ton of implausibilities, some of which i will address in spoilertown below.<br><br>if you are yourself on a stalled train looking for a diversion, this is an excellent choice. okay, that's a bit glib and unfair - this is an entertaining book, but you really need to avoid questioning it, or you're just going to get yourself into a tizzy. it's worth a read, but it's not changing the psych suspense game or anything.<br><br>my gripes follow, and they are spoilery, so don't ruin the book for yourself by clicking, okay?<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ the book wants you to accept that there are tons of lazy men out there who are just waiting for the opportunity to become a murdery rapist and are willing to pay for that opportunity, but don't have the discipline to choose and stalk a victim on their own. <br><br>even taking the criminal element out of the equation, this business plan makes no sense. is it that hard to meet a lady in the more traditional setting of a bar or a club? or even on an online dating service where women are actually looking for a suitor? because judging by the women that were chosen to be unwittingly drawn into this scheme, many of them weren't even available for a relationship. and i'm not sure how knowing a stranger's commuting details gives anyone an advantage in making a connection. life isn't a rom-com, and i would never accept the advances of a stranger who approached me on the subway. that's just urban sensibility 101. so if this was intended to be a dating service, without turning into what it turned into, the subjects were poorly chosen. none of these men are going to want their money back when they discover that their targets are in long-term relationships? what is it they're even paying for? how hard is it to find a pretty girl and track her movements yourself? and maybe i'm just ruined by the unpredictability of the new york subway system, but there ain't nothing certain about my daily commute. every day is an adventure of "when will the train come?" and "how crowded will the platform be?" and "which car will have the unbearably smelly person with no pants on lying down across the entire bank of seats?" you take what you get, and there's no pattern to my commute other than the line, direction and the general time, and even that is fairly flexible.<br><br>once the service <i>became</i> criminal, the business plan makes even less sense. now both parties are relying on the discretion of strangers to cover up their crimes. the men are trusting an anonymous service to cover the tracks they've left in downloading the details of their particular woman and the service itself is trusting the men not to blab to their friends. neither of these are smart trust falls. and putting pictures of real women in the paper is bananas. obviously, someone's going to see themselves or someone they know and start trying to get to the bottom of it. none of this makes any sense to me, but granted - it does make for a gripping tale. <br><br>as far as the whodunnit reveal, that prickles another of my pet peeves - the perfect villain syndrome. yes, i can accept that there are sociopaths out there who are passing; able to blend in without those closest to them knowing that they're one bad day away from being murdered. but really? having two villains here who are both super close to their victims (plural to include katie) and the mask never slipped even once? to go from dinner party to knife-stabby in a heartbeat just seems implausible to me. people have tells. and if they want you dead, literally, you will usually know it.<br><br>also, <i>murder</i> seems a punishment a bit disproportionate to zoe's supposed crimes. not to mention all the other victims, who were guilty of absolutely nothing. i find it hard to fathom that a woman would be down with dispassionately setting up a bunch of completely innocent women to be murdered or sexually assaulted, even with the winky "who, me?" of plausible deniability.<br><br>and a minor point, but zoe's boss getting angry about her terrified reaction when he reaches across her sleeping body to undo her seat belt when he is driving her home, knowing what she's been going through, is completely baffling. even if she wasn't already in a state of fear over the threats she'd been experiencing, it's completely bananas that a man she's not even particularly close to would think it was okay to do that. and to then get offended at her outrage and confusion. that's a pretty intimate gesture, and a hell of a thing to wake up to. a grown-ass woman can unhook her own seat belt, and it was an invasive and unnecessary gesture. was it meant to be a time-saver? bizarre. this is the kind of thing that bothers me as a reader - the only reason it's in there is to cast suspicion on him, and it's an inauthentic situation in any real-world scenario. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="6880700971717625141" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer14012046999694698636">*Thank you to Netgalley and Little Brown Book Group for my ARC in exchange for a fair and honest review*<br/><br/>OMG! Towards the end of this book I felt as if I was standing on the edge of a precipice, my stomach chasing butterflies, and my heart beating fit to burst - but forgive me, I'm getting ahead of myself, because there's much more to come before then.<br/><br/>Nobody thinks too deeply about their daily commute to and from work by Tube, a bit mundane maybe, sometimes stressful, the hustle and bustle, but a</span>
  <span id="freeText14012046999694698636" style="display:none">*Thank you to Netgalley and Little Brown Book Group for my ARC in exchange for a fair and honest review*<br /><br />OMG! Towards the end of this book I felt as if I was standing on the edge of a precipice, my stomach chasing butterflies, and my heart beating fit to burst - but forgive me, I'm getting ahead of myself, because there's much more to come before then.<br /><br />Nobody thinks too deeply about their daily commute to and from work by Tube, a bit mundane maybe, sometimes stressful, the hustle and bustle, but after reading this it would be hard not to see something a bit more sinister in your daily journey. The guy opposite who you catch looking at you, is it just a glance or does he have fantasies about hurting you or worse? <br /><br />When Zoe Walker sees her photo in the classified ads in a London newspaper, she is desperate to find out why it's there, and more importantly who put it there. Worse still it's among the ads for 'escorts' chat lines and dating agencies. And so begins this journey of terror that knows no limits, but I don't want to give anything away because I wouldn't want to spoil the journey for YOU.<br /><br />This is a gripping, cleverly crafted story, that has some jaw dropping moments - and boy I've read more than my fair share of them this year! But along comes 'I See You' and it just darn well blows my socks off! Clare Mackintosh gets right into one's psyche, real deep down, determined to unleash your deepest fears, and she does it wonderfully.<br /><br />Exciting - Shocking - Unbelievably Clever! Read it - you won't be sorry.</span>

<div id="review_1787291425" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1787291425" />
    <a title="Elyse  Walters" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/597461-elyse-walters"><img alt="Elyse  Walters" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514246949p2/597461.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1787291425?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elyse  Walters" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elyse  Walters" href="/user/show/597461-elyse-walters">Elyse  Walters</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1787291425" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1672042901652060816">Clare Mackintosh wrote a 'timely' psychological grabber and crime chiller. In the near future, most people will live in a total surveillance state -- which for some people breeds fear of conformity and stifles free self expression. <br/><br/>This story clearly opens our eyes to the fact that we are living in a fishbowl. <br/>Governments and large corporations have spread cameras, microphones and other tracking devices all across the globe, and they also have the capacity to store and process oceans of surveill</span>
  <span id="freeText1672042901652060816" style="display:none">Clare Mackintosh wrote a 'timely' psychological grabber and crime chiller. In the near future, most people will live in a total surveillance state -- which for some people breeds fear of conformity and stifles free self expression. <br /><br />This story clearly opens our eyes to the fact that we are living in a fishbowl. <br />Governments and large corporations have spread cameras, microphones and other tracking devices all across the globe, and they also have the capacity to store and process oceans of surveillance data in real time. Big brother not only watches our sex life, he analyzes it. Nightmarish! So far, attempts to control surveillance have generally failed.<br />Yes...there 'are' some obvious benefits: reduction of crime and other smaller abuses that go unreported--- but Clare Mackintosh gave us a precautionary story....and it 'is'<br />creepy to think about. <br /><br />Many readers absolutely loved "I let You Go", ( last years much talked about debut mystery crime thriller). I was on the opposite end of that excitement. <br />However...all my complaints about her first book, are gone in this one. I found this book a little more tangible to connect with and more plausible. <br />Think about all the people being watched-- especially women. Normal every day women going about business as if they are invisible to the greater world at large. <br /><br />After Zoe Walker sees her photo in the London Gazette, in the classified section, she is determined to get some answers....especially after immediately the next day the advert shows a photo of another woman.<br /><br />Can you imagine after there have been women murdered since discovering the picture of yourself --- you come to this thought:<br />"What if someone's putting in photo's of women they're going to murder, and I'm next?"<br />Fearful! Would you be able to sleep at night?<br /><br />There's diversity of personalities in the characters. Kelly is an interesting police officer - with he own set of issues-on the London transport. <br />The female characters stand out stronger than the men.....( but what's surprising about that?) lol. <br /><br />As for the ending? You wonder about the twists in these type of stories right? What I liked about it is not only 'who' -- but 'why'. So --even if you think you 'might' know the ending - and do not be so sure ( really: don't)...there's an element added which I found interesting 'with' the ending as much as whodunit. <br /><br />Thank you to Penguin Random House and the Berkley Team for offering me a copy of this book. To be released Feb. 12, 2017. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1672042901652060816" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16800757208855420356" style="display:none">Oh man. I am so bummed. This is not a good follow up to Clare Mackintosh's debut blockbuster, I LET YOU GO. I'm picky, but I loved that book. I even added it to my TWISTER HALL OF FAME shelf!<br /><br /><b>The problems with I SEE YOU:</b><br /><br />First, I figured out the "twisty" ending VERY EARLY in the book. And I'm not usually known for that. <br /><br />Second, the plot was ridiculously unbelievable. The entire story is built on a naive idea that stalkers would pay big money to join a website that would do the stalking for them. Crazy?????? Yes. <br /><br />Third, the story is boring. Preachy. When I read fiction, I don't want to be preached to or bored. <i>Just don't.</i><br /><br />I see my GR friends are giving high ratings to Mackintosh's third book. Let's hope this is simply a sophomore slump!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18380887115562961063">I was so mindful of reading this book. I have come across authors debut novels that have really made an impact on me then their subsequent book has fallen flat, so I opened this with trepidation, but I need not have feared because this author has a talent. <br/><br/>Yep, a real talent that just comes through this book immensely. <br/><br/>She has done it again, she has excelled herself in her writing ability to not just pull you into the book, oh no, you are 'shoved' into it with full force and eagerness, so much s</span>
  <span id="freeText18380887115562961063" style="display:none">I was so mindful of reading this book. I have come across authors debut novels that have really made an impact on me then their subsequent book has fallen flat, so I opened this with trepidation, but I need not have feared because this author has a talent. <br /><br />Yep, a real talent that just comes through this book immensely. <br /><br />She has done it again, she has excelled herself in her writing ability to not just pull you into the book, oh no, you are 'shoved' into it with full force and eagerness, so much so, that its a case of 'one more chapter' one more chapter' and so it goes on until your eyes are dropping.<br /><br />Its a book that stays in your head, just like her debut novel.<br /><br />Zoe, London Underground, CCTV, being tracked, are you being followed. <br /><br />All the characters in this story are so real, from someone who is the main character right down to someone you would feel in life is insignificant.<br /><br />But they are not.<br /><br />This is a thrill ride, this is a 'is someone watching me, if so who'.<br />At times its a scary read, a thrilling read, many bit your nail moments.<br /><br />This is an author that I will be following.<br /><br />My thanks to Little, Brown Book Group UK via Net Galley for my early copy.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780751554120" href="/book/show/28005522-i-see-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7668522-carol?shelf=mystery-crime">mystery-crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7668522-carol?shelf=published-2016">published-2016</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1680645818" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer510366915634727116"><b>Guess who I am....... "I SEE YOU, but you DON'T see me."</b><p>In Clare Macintosh's new mystery-thriller, danger is <b>always</b> lurking around the corner, and 'someone' is <b>always</b> watching as <b>fear</b> overtakes Zoe Walker's everyday life.</p><p>With stalkers and thieves......rapists and murderers, bits of clues here and there kept me guessing and anxiously turning the pages to find the perpetrator of the deadly scheme; <u>but then,</u> at what should have been the most intense climatic moment of the whole story, the blow-by-b</p></span>
  <span id="freeText510366915634727116" style="display:none"><b>Guess who I am....... "I SEE YOU, but you DON'T see me."</b><p>In Clare Macintosh's new mystery-thriller, danger is <b>always</b> lurking around the corner, and 'someone' is <b>always</b> watching as <b>fear</b> overtakes Zoe Walker's everyday life.</p><p>With stalkers and thieves......rapists and murderers, bits of clues here and there kept me guessing and anxiously turning the pages to find the perpetrator of the deadly scheme; <u>but then,</u> at what should have been the most intense climatic moment of the whole story, the blow-by-blow <i>(sadly)</i> falls flat with an unconvincingly written encounter.</p><p>Now, despite my being somewhat disappointed at that crucial point in the plot, <b>I SEE YOU</b> is still a very good police procedural mystery <i>(with a shocking twist)</i> that the reader just 'might' see coming......or not, but <i>(for me)</i> it was just missing that 'big wallop' you find in <b>I LET YOU GO</b></p><p>
  <i>(A few typos and need of editing in my UK copy)</i>
</p></span>

<div id="review_1780740653" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1780740653" />
    <a title="Norma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41400192-norma"><img alt="Norma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589038160p2/41400192.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1780740653?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Norma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Norma" href="/user/show/41400192-norma">Norma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780399586552" href="/book/show/31951280-i-see-you">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1780740653" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14819972253298097059">When I first realized that this author had a new book out I quickly snapped it up as I absolutely loved her first novel I LET YOU GO and was totally shocked with that unforgettable major twist!  Although I have no intentions of comparing the two novels as they are completely different, this one just didn't work out as well for me.<br/><br/>I SEE YOU by CLARE MACKINTOSH is a good mystery/crime thriller that had me engaged, entertained, and interested enough throughout most of this book to keep me turning t</span>
  <span id="freeText14819972253298097059" style="display:none">When I first realized that this author had a new book out I quickly snapped it up as I absolutely loved her first novel I LET YOU GO and was totally shocked with that unforgettable major twist!  Although I have no intentions of comparing the two novels as they are completely different, this one just didn't work out as well for me.<br /><br />I SEE YOU by CLARE MACKINTOSH is a good mystery/crime thriller that had me engaged, entertained, and interested enough throughout most of this book to keep me turning those pages but then it lost me somewhere near the end. In my opinion there was an unnecessary twist with the reveal that just didn't pan out for me as the reasoning behind it just didn't seem all that realistic to me and I had a sneaky suspicion who the culprit was going to be.  So I definitely missed out on the shock-factor of the final reveal. <br /><br />I found the cover and title of this book to be appealing and very fitting which draws you right into this sinister tale of how women are being targeted, watched, and followed while commuting to and from work on the London Underground.<br /><br />CLARE MACKINTOSH delivers a slow-building suspenseful storyline that is well-written and an angst driven read here. I couldn’t even imagine how scared I would be if I seen a picture of myself in the classifieds for a dating site and was one of the women being stalked and followed like our main character Zoe.  Scary! <br /><br />I SEE YOU is told in three different alternating points of view between Zoe Walker, PC Kelly Swift, and the stalker.  PC Kelly Swift was told in the third person and sometimes I found her to be a little confusing when she would be recounting some incidences from her past.<br /><br />To sum it all up it was an entertaining, mostly enjoyable, suspenseful, steady-paced, quick and easy read with a twist ending.<br /><br />Review written and posted on our themed book blog:<br />Two Sisters Lost In A Coulee Reading<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://twosisterslostinacoulee.com">https://twosisterslostinacoulee.com</a><br /><br />Coulee: a term applied rather loosely to different landforms, all of which refer to a kind of valley. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14819972253298097059" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780751566048" href="/book/show/29622552-i-see-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4824134-jules?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4824134-jules?shelf=direct-from-publisher">direct-from-publisher</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4824134-jules?shelf=the-book-club">the-book-club</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1644761924" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7726607774499342916">I found this book really hard to put down, especially the second half, which I lived and breathed until the very last page. I’m sure this thriller made my heart stop beating, not once, but twice, having to briefly stop reading in order to catch my breath. I can feel my heart racing just thinking of a couple of specific moments within the book.<br/><br/>The short chapters written in italics throughout the story were rather creepy and gave me the heebie-jeebies.<br/><br/>It would be misleading of me to say this is in</span>
  <span id="freeText7726607774499342916" style="display:none">I found this book really hard to put down, especially the second half, which I lived and breathed until the very last page. I’m sure this thriller made my heart stop beating, not once, but twice, having to briefly stop reading in order to catch my breath. I can feel my heart racing just thinking of a couple of specific moments within the book.<br /><br />The short chapters written in italics throughout the story were rather creepy and gave me the heebie-jeebies.<br /><br />It would be misleading of me to say this is in any way the same as a TV mini-series I absolutely loved back in the late 1990s called <i>Killer Net</i>, but a couple of things about it really reminded me of it, so made it all that more exciting for me. If you love the idea behind this book, you may wish to watch <i>Killer Net</i>, as I suspect you’ll enjoy it too.<br /><br />Crikey, what an ending to a great thriller... and breathe!<br /><br />This is a psychological crime thriller, and for someone like me, who loves psychological thrillers but isn’t a huge fan of crime and police procedural, I think this had the perfect balance.<br /><br />I would like to thank the publishers for a proof copy of this book, via THE Book Club (TBC) on Facebook, in exchange for an honest review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7726607774499342916" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Esil" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Esil" href="/user/show/3643764-esil">Esil</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1790752507" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5992794699015047993">3+ stars. I can't bring myself to give I See You 4 stars. There were a few too many things that bugged me. But it's definitely a tad higher than a 3 star read. I See You starts with middle aged mother of young adults Zoe seeing a photo of herself in the dating service section of a newspaper. She ends up in contact with police officer Kelly. And the story unfolds from both their points of view. I can't say any more to avoid spoilers.<br/><br/>Some strengths:<br/>-Near the beginning in a brief interlude, the unk</span>
  <span id="freeText5992794699015047993" style="display:none">3+ stars. I can't bring myself to give I See You 4 stars. There were a few too many things that bugged me. But it's definitely a tad higher than a 3 star read. I See You starts with middle aged mother of young adults Zoe seeing a photo of herself in the dating service section of a newspaper. She ends up in contact with police officer Kelly. And the story unfolds from both their points of view. I can't say any more to avoid spoilers.<br /><br />Some strengths:<br />-Near the beginning in a brief interlude, the unknown perpetrator declares "Routine will kill you". I loved that MacKintosh's book plays with the reality for urban commuters -- jammed together on subways, buses and streetcars everyday with the same people, but somehow assuming anonymity as we all pretend we're somewhere else through phones, books, daydreams or sleep.<br />-I liked Kelly. She reminded me a bit of Havers in Elizabeth George's Linley and Havers series -- well meaning and smart, but often overly eager.<br />-I didn't love Zoe as a character, but I did like the interactions with her various family members.<br />-The very end was clever, although awfully disturbing.<br /><br />What bugged me:<br />-I never quite bought into the purpose for which Zoe and other women's photos ended up in the dating service section of the newspaper without their knowledge.<br />-Although generally very readable, the middle of I See You felt kind of slack and aimless.<br />-The "who" part of the resolution irked me. It didn't ring true.<br /><br />Not a waste of time, but definitely not a favourite read. Many GR friends loved Mackintosh's I Let You Go, which I haven't read. I would definitely give it a try based on what I liked in I See You. Thanks to Netgalley and the publisher for an opportunity to read an advance copy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5992794699015047993" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1641628487" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1641628487" />
    <a title="Linda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9472704-linda"><img alt="Linda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1336837712p2/9472704.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1641628487?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linda" href="/user/show/9472704-linda">Linda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9472704-linda?shelf=mystery-thrillers">mystery-thrillers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1641628487" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14156831362251751348">"If it's just the two of you. Just you, and whoever's behind you. Whoever is chasing you. How fast could you run then?"<br/><br/>Zoe Walker is a deep creature of habit. She leaves the house at the same time every day and boards the same train every day. She even pinpoints her favorite seats and standing positions while pinned together, elbow to elbow and leg to leg, ready to hit the opening door and escape the madness held within.<br/><br/>But something shocking catches her attention while perusing the local paper.</span>
  <span id="freeText14156831362251751348" style="display:none">"If it's just the two of you. Just you, and whoever's behind you. Whoever is chasing you. How fast could you run then?"<br /><br />Zoe Walker is a deep creature of habit. She leaves the house at the same time every day and boards the same train every day. She even pinpoints her favorite seats and standing positions while pinned together, elbow to elbow and leg to leg, ready to hit the opening door and escape the madness held within.<br /><br />But something shocking catches her attention while perusing the local paper. It's an advertisement for a hook-up website with her own photo staring back at her. Could this even be possible or is it just a trick of the eye? Zoe dismisses it and resumes her regular family life with her two adult children, Katie and Justin, and her live-in boyfriend, Simon.<br /><br />But as the days goes by, Zoe has the odd feeling that she's being followed. She contacts the police and a young officer, Kelly, actually believes her. Together, they dog behind this case as the "normal" quickly flips into an "abnormal zone".<br /><br />Well, now. First and foremost, I am an avid fan of Clare Mackintosh. Her first book, I Let You Go, was so outstanding. That is a hard act to follow even when you're the actual author. Mackintosh has done mega research here in online websites, social media, and police procedures. Perhaps that's part of my lukewarm reaction to this one. When you lead with what you know rather than what the characters feel and how they react with mounting intensity, there lies the problem.<br /><br />We were able to walk around inside the heads of her highly developed characters in I Let You Go. We related to the slanted walkways in which these individuals fought to balance themselves under unimaginable circumstances. I See You seemed to follow more of a precise formula that drove the storyline and its outcome. It didn't hold me to the page as her first book did.<br /><br />It's still a worthy read, however. There's the brillance of the Mackintosh writing here in place and time. My greatest wish is for a return to her uncanny ability to hold her finger on the pulse of her characters, once more, in her next offering. No reader can resist the vicarious experience of another's heartbeat from slow and steady to rapid and pounding.<br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="14156831362251751348" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1850239455" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1850239455" />
    <a title="Karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12851291-karen"><img alt="Karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555906256p2/12851291.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781101988299" href="/book/show/31160324-i-see-you">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1850239455" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11954819602529672767">So this book wasn't great but kept me turning pages and entertained. When I got towards the part to reveal who was behind this mess, the reason just didn't seem realistic at all. This was good on showing police procedure, and I did really like Kelly, the woman cop.</span>

<div id="review_1821664688" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1821664688" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1821664688?book_show_action=true">Nov 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780399586552" href="/book/show/31951280-i-see-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1821664688" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7532027188318552996">I would probably have liked ‘‘I See You’’ better if it were less of a commercialized novel. <br/><br/>Alright, so I know most books are written for some kind of gain – money – but not many actually feel that way.<br/><br/>It’s rare for me to even think in such terms. Obviously, I’m aware during the reading part if a novel/series was written for our entertaining alone or to convey a certain message.<br/><br/>So because I didn’t find ‘‘I See You’’ full of deeply explored themes, my mind goes immediately to that one (cringe-wor</span>
  <span id="freeText7532027188318552996" style="display:none">I would probably have liked ‘‘I See You’’ better if it were less of a commercialized novel. <br /><br />Alright, so I know most books are written for some kind of gain – money – but not many actually feel that way.<br /><br />It’s rare for me to even think in such terms. Obviously, I’m aware during the reading part if a novel/series was written for our entertaining alone or to convey a certain message.<br /><br />So because I didn’t find ‘‘I See You’’ full of deeply explored themes, my mind goes immediately to that one (cringe-worthy) adjective. <br /><br />I’m not saying that the author really only thought about the profit she would make when writing this, I’m saying it doesn’t teach us much and it’s not that complex of a mystery.<br /><br />Plus to me it felt like some things were exaggerated – for instance, it’s true that the metro is not the safest place on Earth, but it’s not that bad and people are not constantly staring at you, since they’re much more focused on their phones. Unless it’s different in London, I don’t know much about that place, sadly.<br /><br />In this book, women are rapped then killed by men who download their information on a website and follow them around to corner them in order to proceed with their vile intentions. <br /><br />Chills. <br /><br />It’s part ‘‘The Girl on the Train,’’ because of all the doubts in the main character’s mind and part the Mason Girls case, because of the murders executed by the clients and the mastermind behind the website.<br /><br />I’m somewhat pleased with the writing, the characterizations and the fast-pacing, but I’m also somewhat displeased with how dramatic the author sometimes is in her writing, how ridiculously the characters act sometimes and how hard it tries to be suspenseful… but fails miserably. <br /><br />The ending is also very despicable. <br /><br />But while the story is relatively familiar, it still manages to be original. And it IS a page-turner. <br /><br />It just very, very much feels like a commercialized book.<br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7532027188318552996" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText4603244629844356625" style="display:none">Thank you to Net Galley, the publishers and to Clare the author for an ARC copy for review.<br /><br />Firstly, I loved Clare's first book a fantastic first novel, the second keeps to the same standard.<br /><br />A powerful, chilling, gripping tense thriller that keeps you guessing all the way.<br /><br />When Zoe Walker sees her photo in the classifieds section of a London newspaper, she is determined to find out why it's there. There's no explanation: just a website, a grainy image and a phone number. She takes it home to her family, who are convinced it's just someone who looks like Zoe. But the next day the advert shows a photo of a different woman, and another the day after that.<br /><br />Is it a mistake? A coincidence? Or is someone keeping track of every move they make . . .<br /><br />I See You is an edge-of-your-seat, page-turning psychological thriller from one of the most exciting and successful British debut talents of 2015!<br /><br />Frightening that this could be so easily be true! <br /><br />Very powerful story, chilling, and gripping, like her debut author a book so powerful it stays in your head, are you being watched?<br /><br />Clare has done such a good job to keep up her high, no excellent standard of her first book, now cannot wait for her next book. Quickly becoming one of Britain's great authors.<br /><br />This book grips you to the very last page, great characters enjoyed Zoe character but also Kelly.<br /><br />Highly recommended and a five star from me.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1696441533" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1696441533" />
    <a title="Taryn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1334938-taryn"><img alt="Taryn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1407768387p2/1334938.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1696441533?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Taryn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Taryn" href="/user/show/1334938-taryn">Taryn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781101988299" href="/book/show/31160324-i-see-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1334938-taryn?shelf=received-from-publisher">received-from-publisher</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1334938-taryn?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1334938-taryn?shelf=mystery-suspense-thriller">mystery-suspense-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1696441533" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6512128658382385564"><blockquote>
  <em>Routine is comforting to you. It’s familiar, reassuring. Routine makes you feel safe. Routine will kill you.</em>
</blockquote><br/><br/>A new thriller from the author of the bestseller <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23125266.I_Let_You_Go' title='I Let You Go by Clare Mackintosh' rel='nofollow noopener'> I Let You Go</a>. What would you do if you discovered a photo of yourself being used to advertise a business that you'd never heard of? Zoe is flipping through the newspaper during her evening commute when she spots a photo of herself in the classifieds section. It's part of an ad for FindtheOne.com, a service she never signed up for. Zoe's</span>
  <span id="freeText6512128658382385564" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <em>Routine is comforting to you. It’s familiar, reassuring. Routine makes you feel safe. Routine will kill you.</em>
</blockquote><br /><br />A new thriller from the author of the bestseller <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23125266.I_Let_You_Go" title="I Let You Go by Clare Mackintosh" rel="nofollow noopener"> I Let You Go</a>. What would you do if you discovered a photo of yourself being used to advertise a business that you'd never heard of? Zoe is flipping through the newspaper during her evening commute when she spots a photo of herself in the classifieds section. It's part of an ad for FindtheOne.com, a service she never signed up for. Zoe's family assures her the photo is of someone who only vaguely resembles her. They try to convince her that there's nothing to worry about, but she can't shake the nagging feeling that something is wrong. She finds similar ads in other issues of the newspaper, each featuring a different woman. She's shocked to recognize a couple of the women as victims of local crimes. Is it a coincidence or could she be next?<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>I see you. But you don’t see me. You’re engrossed in your book; a paperback cover with a girl in a red dress. I can’t see the title but it doesn’t matter; they’re all the same. If it isn’t boy meets girl, it’s boy stalks girl. Boy kills girl. The irony isn’t lost on me.</em>
</blockquote><br /><br />The story alternates between Zoe Walker's personal life (first person) and PC Kelly Swift's investigation (third person), with occasional interludes from a potential stalker (second person).<br /><br />• Zoe is a single mom who lives with her devoted boyfriend and her two adult children. Her daughter is an aspiring actress and her son's life is finally back on track after some youthful indiscretions. <strong>Zoe is dull</strong>, but we spend the most time with her character. Her rationalization of her ex-husband's past behavior and her ill-advised antics annoyed me. There's a lot of focus on her personal problems. While the lack of action in the first half did make me question whether Zoe's paranoia was warranted, the focus on the banalities of her domestic life made the story feel <strong>slow-paced</strong>.<br /><br />• Kelly takes an interest in the classified ads after Zoe alerts her to a possible connection to the case she's been working on. Finding a connection between the classified ads and other crimes could help her redeem herself. Four years ago, she was demoted from the Sexual Offenses Team to the Neighborhood Policing Team. <strong>I loved Kelly's passion for her profession and her protectiveness of her twin sister.</strong> She has a victim-focused approach to police work, but she also has issues getting too close to her cases. I was rooting for her! I wish Zoe and Kelly interacted more, because I would have liked to spend more time with her.<br /><br />• The stalker's sections are short, but unnerving. I love how Mackintosh writes sociopaths. It puts me on edge!<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>I wanted reassurance. I wanted to be told I was overreacting; paranoid; delusional. I wanted false promises and glasses-half-full. A few days ago I worried the police weren’t taking me seriously; now I’m worried because they are.</em>
</blockquote><br /><br />The creepiest parts take place in the claustrophobic London Underground. We never know who might be lurking around the corner, watching our every move, and waiting for the right moment to strike. The crowds and cameras in the tunnels lulled Zoe into <strong>complacency</strong>. There's a <strong>false sense of security </strong>because there are so many potential witnesses, but everyone is caught up in their own lives and gadgets, oblivious to the world around them. The popularity of social media adds extra concerns. How much of the information we voluntarily publicize can be used against us? There's also an important lesson about <strong>being vigilant and trusting your instincts</strong>. There are a few instances where women’s <strong>concerns are dismissed as paranoia or overreacting. They're asked to ignore the clear evidence in front of them.</strong> This story shows how easy it can be to dismiss our own fears, either because of outside pressure or our own desire to feel safe. On the investigative side, Kelly has to question her approach towards victims. Is a victim under any obligation to assist the investigation? Should a victim be pressured to testify against their will?<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“Offenders, coppers, witnesses, victims … there’s one common thread running through them all, Kelly, and it’s that no two people are the same. Every victim deals differently with what’s happened to them; some are hell-bent on revenge, others want justice, some are looking for closure, and some”—he looked her straight in the eye—“some just want to move on.”</em>
</blockquote><br /><br /><em>I See You </em>uses an exaggerated situation to remind us of the risks we might encounter in our everyday lives. The paranoia and anxiety increases as Zoe goes from being unsure if she has anything to worry about to feeling hunted. <strong>It's an unsettling reminder to stay alert, trust your intuition, and be aware of your surroundings. </strong>Whether you like this one will depend on what you want out of your thrillers. My feelings for <em>I See You</em> are similar to my feelings for David Bell's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27190380-since-she-went-away?from_search=true" rel="nofollow noopener">Since You Went Away</a>. I tend to prefer investigations or sociopaths over the parenting of teenagers, but there are always exceptions! <strong>This book was entertaining and I suspected almost everyone at one point, but I didn't feel like I was at the center of the action.</strong><br /><br />_____________<br /><b>I received this book for free from Netgalley &amp; Berkley in exchange for an honest review. This does not affect my opinion of the book or the content of my review.The publication date is February 21, 2017.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="6512128658382385564" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780399586552" href="/book/show/31951280-i-see-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/372001-dana-kenedy-dana-and-the-books?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/372001-dana-kenedy-dana-and-the-books?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/372001-dana-kenedy-dana-and-the-books?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1805753578" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2284663422554350692">3.5/5 - This review can also be found on my blog, <a href='http://wp.me/p6sNGI-nO' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dana and the Books</a><br/><br/>Who's the bad guy? That's the question on everyone's mind when flipping through thrillers. Sometimes, the answer is so painfully obvious it's embarrassing, and other times you're guessing until the final word. Thankfully,<em> I See You</em> fell into the latter. I was 100% convinced it was Person X and I don't think I've ever been happier to have been wrong.<br/><br/><em>I See You</em> is a novel you can breeze through easily in an afternoon. The first cha</span>
  <span id="freeText2284663422554350692" style="display:none">3.5/5 - This review can also be found on my blog, <a href="http://wp.me/p6sNGI-nO" rel="nofollow noopener">Dana and the Books</a><br /><br />Who's the bad guy? That's the question on everyone's mind when flipping through thrillers. Sometimes, the answer is so painfully obvious it's embarrassing, and other times you're guessing until the final word. Thankfully,<em> I See You</em> fell into the latter. I was 100% convinced it was Person X and I don't think I've ever been happier to have been wrong.<br /><br /><em>I See You</em> is a novel you can breeze through easily in an afternoon. The first chapters were a bit on the rough side with too many unnecessary tangents from main character Zoe's point of view. However, that may have been intentional. Zoe wasn't supposed to be exciting. She was supposed to be a mundane, dull, average woman going about her day-to-day life. It was when Zoe got thrust out of her comfortable world into a whirlwind of panic that the story began to shine.<br /><br />We get introduced to Kelly, the police officer investigating Zoe's case, and she steals the story. In fact, I wish we had a few extra chapters with Kelly as the focus as she felt a much stronger character than Zoe; Kelly's chapters had a bit more substance and mystery. She was a tough character with a complicated past that seeped into her present.<br /><br />I'm not a fan of dual-POVs where the characters aren't narrated in the same POV—Zoe's chapters were in first person and Kelly's in third person. For me, I would have enjoyed the story more if both characters were in third person. Zoe's internal thinkings slowed the book down, making it a bit monotonous in a few areas where the tension could have been ramped up.<br /><br />However, with that said, the tension is fantastic! It built up without me noticing, and I had to take a small break when when my knuckles turned white from clutching my book too hard. After a few cups of much needed tea, I finished the book in one go for a superb finale!<br /><br />Maybe you're all better at guessing who culprits are, but I'm SO happy I didn't figure it out. That killer twist in the last chapter made it all worthwhile.<br /><br />Want some thrills in your life? Pick up a copy:  (<a href="https://www.bookdepository.com/I-See-You-Clare-Mackintosh/9780751554144/?a_aid=DanaAndTheBooks" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Depository</a> / <a href="http://amzn.to/2k04XLm" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon US</a> / <a href="http://amzn.to/2juiTJP" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon Canada</a> / <a href="http://amzn.to/2judrqJ" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon UK</a>)<br /><br />Thanks so much to Berkley Publishing for sending over a copy!<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2284663422554350692" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42481357-melisa?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42481357-melisa?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42481357-melisa?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1641599562" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8849165259886613708">Here's the thing about this book: it is a very strong thriller on its own, however I had such high expectations after reading Mackintosh's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23125266-i-let-you-go?from_search=true' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>I Let You Go</a>, I can't begin to compare. <b>I Let You Go</b> ripped my heart out and stomped it into a million pieces. While still a great book, I did not get anywhere near that dramatic reaction from this one. So my rating is skewed a bit due to my personal experience.<br/><br/>Clare Mackintosh is an extremely talented writer, she has crafted a fast-paced, well-developed plot</span>
  <span id="freeText8849165259886613708" style="display:none">Here's the thing about this book: it is a very strong thriller on its own, however I had such high expectations after reading Mackintosh's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23125266-i-let-you-go?from_search=true" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">I Let You Go</a>, I can't begin to compare. <b>I Let You Go</b> ripped my heart out and stomped it into a million pieces. While still a great book, I did not get anywhere near that dramatic reaction from this one. So my rating is skewed a bit due to my personal experience.<br /><br />Clare Mackintosh is an extremely talented writer, she has crafted a fast-paced, well-developed plot. This felt more like a police procedural rather than a thriller at times, but both aspects of the plot are extremely well-researched and thought out. <br /><br />While the reader is constantly second guessing every character, I did in the end, figure out the culprit, but then...BAM. In true Clare Mackintosh style she twists everything you thought was true and makes you look at everything in a different light.<br /><br />I'm giving this one 3.5 stars rounded up to 4 because I loved the writing and I couldn't put it down. <br /><br />Thank you to the publisher and Netgalley for a copy of this book in exchange for an honest review.<br /><br />You can also find this review on my blog at <a href="https://thebookcollective.net/2016/10/25/i-see-you-by-clare-mackintosh/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">The Book Collective</a>.</span>

          </span>

        <a title="Lindsay - Traveling Sisters Book Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsay - Traveling Sisters Book Reviews" href="/user/show/54886546-lindsay---traveling-sisters-book-reviews">Lindsay - Traveling Sisters Book Reviews</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1699162823" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11532930634761910117">3.5 stars. That final ending really took me by surprise! By far, it was the best part of the story and made me add another half star to my rating. In my opinion, this novel was not as good as the author's debut, 'I Let You Go'.<br/><br/>This book started off strong until about the halfway point when it started to get repetitive and lost its thrilling edge. The story focuses on the idea of being watched - not just a simple stalker situation, but an entire system of technology and surveillance watching your</span>
  <span id="freeText11532930634761910117" style="display:none">3.5 stars. That final ending really took me by surprise! By far, it was the best part of the story and made me add another half star to my rating. In my opinion, this novel was not as good as the author's debut, 'I Let You Go'.<br /><br />This book started off strong until about the halfway point when it started to get repetitive and lost its thrilling edge. The story focuses on the idea of being watched - not just a simple stalker situation, but an entire system of technology and surveillance watching your every move. It is a terrifying concept and had me feeling tense for the first half of the novel. I really liked the main character, Zoe, and felt empathy for her situation, however, there were a few circumstances where it seemed like she took unnecessary risks and was slightly unrealistic for me. I felt the 'guilty party' was a bit over-the-top and their motivation was somewhat far-fetched, but after reading that last twist on the final page, the shock factor went up for me and things seemed to fall into place a little better.<br /><br />This book really made me 'think' and analyze my life and the idea of being watched. The 'dating business' that is introduced within this story horrifies me. Could this really happen? It's one of those books that makes you worry that it could be happening in your own life. Scary!! I'll be checking over my shoulder in public for the next while.......</span>

<div id="review_1669109521" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1669109521" />
    <a title="Liz Barnsley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16471876-liz-barnsley"><img alt="Liz Barnsley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1447272680p2/16471876.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1669109521?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz Barnsley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz Barnsley" href="/user/show/16471876-liz-barnsley">Liz Barnsley</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16471876-liz-barnsley?shelf=received-from-publisher">received-from-publisher</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16471876-liz-barnsley?shelf=highly-recommended">highly-recommended</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16471876-liz-barnsley?shelf=top-psychological-thriller">top-psychological-thriller</a>
